title="Belarus">Belarus</a></span></th><td>116 (2009 census)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Turkmenistan"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkmenistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a></span></th><td>54 (1995 census)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Latvia"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a></span></th><td>52 (2019 statistics)<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Languages</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian</a><br />(<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">West Adyghe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabardian_language" title="Kabardian language">Kabardian Adyghe</a>, extinct <a href="/wiki/Ubykh_language" title="Ubykh language">Ubykh Adyghe</a> dialects), also <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Religion</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Predominantly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a><br />Minority <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Greenwood_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenwood-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a><sup id="cite_ref-Sreda_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sreda-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and Circassian ethnic faith <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_Habze" title="Adyghe Habze">Khabzeism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2012maps_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012maps-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> as well as atheists<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Related ethnic groups</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Abazgi (<a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz people">Abkhaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abazin" class="mw-redirect" title="Abazin">Abazin</a>)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Circassians</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Черкесы</span> <i>Čerkesy</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Çerkesler</i>), also known by their <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a> <b>Adyghe</b> (<a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian</a>: Адыгэхэр <i>Adygekher</i>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Ады́ги</span> <i>Adýgi</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Adığeler</i>), are a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages" title="Northwest Caucasian languages">Northwest Caucasian</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> ethnic group native to <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">Circassia</a>, many of whom were <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic cleansing of Circassians">displaced</a> in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_War" title="Caucasian War">Russian conquest of the Caucasus</a> in the 19th century, especially after the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Circassian_War" title="Russo-Circassian War">Russo-Circassian War</a> in 1864.  The Circassians mainly speak the <a href="/wiki/Circassian_languages" title="Circassian languages">Circassian languages</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages" title="Northwest Caucasian languages">Northwest Caucasian</a> <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> with three main dialects and numerous sub-dialects. Many Circassians also speak <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>, having been <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiled</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> to lands of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, where the majority of them today live.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="this is likely not accurate, many Circassian languages are dying out, and many Circassians don&#39;t speak any Circassian language (May 2017)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Most Circassians are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In its narrowest sense, the term "Circassian" includes the twelve historic <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_people" title="Adyghe people">Adyghe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian</a>: Адыгэ, <i>Adyge</i>) princedoms of Circassia (three democratic and nine aristocratic); <a href="/wiki/Abdzakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdzakh">Abdzakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Besleney" title="Besleney">Besleney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bzhedug" class="mw-redirect" title="Bzhedug">Bzhedug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatuqwai" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatuqwai">Hatuqwai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamkhegh" title="Mamkhegh">Mamkhegh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natukhai" class="mw-redirect" title="Natukhai">Natukhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shapsug" class="mw-redirect" title="Shapsug">Shapsug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temirgoy" class="mw-redirect" title="Temirgoy">Temirgoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubykh_people" title="Ubykh people">Ubykh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yegeruqwai" title="Yegeruqwai">Yegeruqwai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhaney" title="Zhaney">Zhaney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> each star on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Adygea" title="Flag of Adygea">Circassian flag</a> representing each princedom.
</p><p>Historical Circassia has been divided by Soviet and Russian administrations into the modern-day titular Circassian republics of <a href="/wiki/Adygea" title="Adygea">Adygea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabardino-Balkaria" title="Kabardino-Balkaria">Kabardino-Balkaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachay-Cherkessia" title="Karachay-Cherkessia">Karachay-Cherkessia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai" title="Krasnodar Krai">Krasnodar Krai</a>, as well as southwestern parts of <a href="/wiki/Stavropol_Krai" title="Stavropol Krai">Stavropol Krai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rostov_Oblast" title="Rostov Oblast">Rostov Oblast</a>. Accordingly, Circassians or Adyghe have also been designated as the following: <i>Adygeans</i> in Adygea, <i>Kabardians</i> in Kabardino-Balkaria, <i><a href="/wiki/Cherkess" title="Cherkess">Cherkess</a></i> in Karachay-Cherkessia,and <i>Shapsug</i> in Krasnodar Krai, although all four are essentially the same people. About 800,000 Circassians remain in historical Circassia, while others live in the Russian Federation outside these <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a>. The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Russia" title="Demographics of Russia">Russian Census</a> recorded 718,727 Circassians, of whom 516,826 are Kabardian, 124,835 are other Adyghe in Adygea, 73,184 are Cherkess and 3,882 Shapsug.<sup id="cite_ref-RussiaCensus_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussiaCensus-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Unrepresented_Nations_and_Peoples_Organization" title="Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization">Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization</a> estimated in the early 1990s that there are as many as 3.7 million "ethnic Circassian" <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> (in over 50 countries)<sup id="cite_ref-UNPO_Yearbook_1997_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO_Yearbook_1997-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> outside the titular Circassian republics (meaning that only one in seven "ethnic Circassians" live in the homeland), and that, of these 3.7 million, more than 2 million live in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-UNPO_Yearbook_1997_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO_Yearbook_1997-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> 300,000 in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> (mostly modern-day <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and 50,000 in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.
</p>
