<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnonyms">Ethnonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ethnonyms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adyghe">Adyghe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Adyghe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg/170px-Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg/255px-Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg/340px-Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parsons._Circassian_Warrior._1862.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Circassian warrior</div></div></div>
<p>The Circassians <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">refer to themselves</a> as <i>Adyghe</i> (also transliterated as <i>Adyga</i>, <i>Adyge</i>, <i>Adygei</i>, <i>Adyghe</i>, <i>Attéghéi</i>). The name is believed to derive from <i>atté</i> "height" to signify a mountaineer or a highlander, and <i>ghéi</i> "sea", signifying "a people dwelling and inhabiting a mountainous country near the sea coast", or "between two seas".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_c_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_c-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Circassian.2C_Charkas.2C_Cherkes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Circassian,_Charkas,_Cherkes">Circassian, Charkas, Cherkes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Circassian, Charkas, Cherkes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The word "Circassians" (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">sər-<span style="font-size:90%">KASS</span>-ee-ənz</i></a>) is an <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonym</a>. The Russians referred to all Circassian tribes as <i>Cherkesy</i>, which may be derived from <i>Kerkety</i>, the name of one of the Adyghe tribes native to the northwestern Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In early <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> sources, the Circassians are referred to as <i>Kasogi</i>, whereas in medieval <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> sources, <i>Kasogi</i> is written as <i>Jarkas</i> and <i>Jahārkas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The spelling <i>Charkas</i> may be an abbreviation of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> <i>Chahār-kas</i> ("four people"), denoting four tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Though "Jahārkas" was used by <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> (died 1406) and <a href="/wiki/Ali_ibn_al-Athir" title="Ali ibn al-Athir">Ali ibn al-Athir</a> (died c. 1232/3), the Persian hypothesis remains uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 10th century, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> referred to the Circassians as <i>Kashak</i>, which appears to be a <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> word derived from <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossetian</a> <i>Kasogi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a> referred to the Circassians as <i>Cherkas</i>, a name which had come into common use by the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This designation (<i>Cherkas</i>) originally "did not designate the Adygei but rather the people living in southern Ukraine".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Even in contemporary times, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> has a province named <a href="/wiki/Cherkasy_Oblast" title="Cherkasy Oblast">Cherkessk</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Cherkasy" title="Cherkasy">its provincial capital</a> bearing the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> in the 13th century, the designation <i>Cherkess</i> "came to refer to the Adygei who remained in the Caucasus, and then became a generic term for all who lived there".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This in turn created terminology "anomalies", and as a result, <i>Cherkes</i> became often used alongside other names such as <i>Adygei</i>, <i>Abaza</i>, <i>Kabardian</i>, <i>Karachay</i>, and <i>Abkhaz</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In Medieval Oriental and European texts, "the Adygei people were known by the name Cherkess/Circassians".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Encyclopaedia Islamica</i> adds: "This is because the Cherkess, the Kabardians and the Adygei people share a common language, which is spoken by the north-western Caucasian (Abkhazi) people, and belongs to the family known as Abkhazian-Adygei".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami_34-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERezaHirtensteinGholami-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In Persian sources, <i>Charkas/Cherkes</i> is used to refer to the "actual" Circassians of the northwest Caucasus, and in some occasions as a general designation for <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">Caucasians</a> who live beyond <a href="/wiki/Derbent" title="Derbent">Derbent</a> (Darband).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManzHaneda1990816–819_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManzHaneda1990816–819-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Russian historiography the term had been used as an exonym for Russian, Ukrainian and <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossack</a> people at least until the end of the 18th century,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and Caucasian Tatar peoples (namely <a href="/w/index.php?title=Terek_Tatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Terek Tatar (page does not exist)">Terek Tatar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kumyks" title="Kumyks">Kumyk</a><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>).
</p><p>In Turkey the term nowadays used as a name for all Caucasian nations such as, such as <a href="/wiki/Karachays" title="Karachays">Karachays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>, different <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestanian</a> diasporas and others.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_policy">Soviet policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Soviet policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite a common self-designation and a common Russian name,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Soviet" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet">Soviet</a> authorities applied four designations to Circassians:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardian</a>, Circassians of <a href="/wiki/Kabardino-Balkaria" title="Kabardino-Balkaria">Kabardino-Balkaria</a> (Circassians speaking the <a href="/wiki/Kabardian_language" title="Kabardian language">Kabardian language</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEВсероссийская_перепись_2010,_Итоги_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEВсероссийская_перепись_2010,_Итоги-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gks.ru_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gks.ru-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> one of two indigenous peoples of the republic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cherkess" title="Cherkess">Cherkess</a> (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Шэрджэс</span> <i>Šărdžăs</i>), Circassians of <a href="/wiki/Karachay-Cherkessia" title="Karachay-Cherkessia">Karachay-Cherkessia</a> (Circassians speaking the <a href="/wiki/Cherkess_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherkess language">Cherkess</a>, i.e. Circassian, language<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEВсероссийская_перепись_2010,_Итоги_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEВсероссийская_перепись_2010,_Итоги-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gks.ru_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gks.ru-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> one of two indigenous peoples of the republic who are mostly <a href="/wiki/Besleney" title="Besleney">Besleney</a> Kabardians. The name "Cherkess" is the Russian form of "Circassian" and was used for all Circassians before Soviet times.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adyghe_people" title="Adyghe people">Adyghe</a> or Adygeans, the indigenous population of the <a href="/wiki/Kuban" title="Kuban">Kuban</a> including <a href="/wiki/Adygea" title="Adygea">Adygea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai" title="Krasnodar Krai">Krasnodar Krai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shapsug" class="mw-redirect" title="Shapsug">Shapsug</a>, the indigenous historical inhabitants of Shapsugia. They live in the <a href="/wiki/Tuapse_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuapse District">Tuapse District</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lazarevsky_City_District" title="Lazarevsky City District">Lazarevsky City District</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/Shapsugsky_National_District" title="Shapsugsky National District">Shapsugsky National District</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a>, both in <a href="/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai" title="Krasnodar Krai">Krasnodar Krai</a> and in Adygea.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Genetically, the Adyghe have shared ancestry partially with neighboring <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">peoples of the Caucasus</a>, with some influence from the other regions.<sup id="cite_ref-Li2008_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Li2008-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian language</a>, also known as Cherkess, is a member of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages" title="Northwest Caucasian languages">Northwest Caucasian language family</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">Archaeological</a> findings, mainly of <a href="/wiki/Dolmens_of_North_Caucasus" title="Dolmens of North Caucasus">dolmens in Northwest Caucasus region</a>, indicate a <a href="/wiki/Megalithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalithic">megalithic</a> culture in the Northwest Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-c.ssianmuseum.co.il_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c.ssianmuseum.co.il-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_period">Medieval period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Medieval period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a result of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> influence, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> spread throughout the Caucasus between the 3rd and 5th centuries AD.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ab_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ab-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> During that period the Circassians (referred to at the time as <i>Kassogs</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-Jaimoukha2005_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jaimoukha2005-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> began to accept Christianity as a national religion, but did not abandon all elements of their indigenous religious beliefs.
</p><p>From around 400 AD wave after wave of invaders began to invade the lands of the <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_people" title="Adyghe people">Adyghe people</a>, who were also known as the <i>Kasogi</i> (or Kassogs) at the time. They were conquered first by the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> (who originated on the Central Asian <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>). Outsiders sometimes confused the Adyghe people with the similarly-named <a href="/wiki/Utigurs" title="Utigurs">Utigurs</a> (a branch of the Bulgars), and both peoples were sometimes conflated under misnomers such as "<i>Utige</i>". Following the dissolution of the Khazar state, the Adyghe people were integrated around the end of the 1st millennium AD into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Alania" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Alania">Kingdom of Alania</a>.
</p><p>Between the 10th and 13th centuries <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> had influence on the Adyghe Circassian peoples, with many adopting <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG/170px-Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG/255px-Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG/340px-Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG 2x" data-file-width="606" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleksey_Mikhailovich_Tcherkassky.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexey_Cherkassky" title="Alexey Cherkassky">Alexey Cherkassky</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Russian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of the Russian Empire">Chancellor of the Russian Empire</a>, descended from the sovereign rulers of <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">Circassia</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 17th century, under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, large numbers of Circassians converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Russia" title="Islam in Russia">Islam</a> from <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1708, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qaplan_I_Giray&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qaplan I Giray (page does not exist)">Qaplan I Giray</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD_I_%D0%93%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9" class="extiw" title="ru:Каплан I Герай">ru</a>&#93;</span>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Crimean_khans" title="List of Crimean khans">Crimean khan</a>, ordered to have 4,000 Kabardian slaves while ascending to the throne. Kabardians led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kurgoko_Atazhukin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kurgoko Atazhukin (page does not exist)">Kurgoko Atazhukin</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%90%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD" class="extiw" title="ru:Кургоко Атажукин">ru</a>&#93;</span> were reluctant to pay tribute to the Crimean Khan.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Qaplan I Giray along with 20,000 warriors marched to Kabarday to retrieve his demands. While setting a fire camp, Crimean Tatars were attacked by 7,000 cavalry units headed by Prince Kurgoko Atazhukin in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Kinzhal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Kinzhal (page does not exist)">battle of Kinzhal</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B0" class="extiw" title="ru:Канжальская битва">ru</a>&#93;</span> near <a href="/wiki/Malka_River" title="Malka River">Malka River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Crimean army was destroyed in one night on 17 September 1708. Only a small group of Crimeans headed by Qaplan I Giray managed to escape.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the Institute of Russian History of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> recognized that the battle of Kinzhal Mountain with the paramount importance in the national history of Kabardians, Balkarians and Ossetians.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_invasion_of_Circassia">Russian invasion of Circassia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Russian invasion of Circassia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Circassian_genocide" title="Circassian genocide">Circassian genocide</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Circassian_nationalism" title="Circassian nationalism">Circassian nationalism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg/220px-Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg/330px-Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg/440px-Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1782" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Resettlement_of_Circassians_Into_Ottoman_Empire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the expulsion of Circassians to the Ottoman Empire. The light-green area denotes the final borders of Circassians who had already been pushed southwards prior to their expulsion to the Ottoman Empire. Note that in the late 18th century the Circassians lost their northern territories, which do not appear in green on this map.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg/200px-Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg/300px-Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg/400px-Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1309" data-file-height="1685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meccan_merchant_and_his_Circassian_slave.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Meccan</a> merchant (right) and his <a href="/wiki/Circassian_nationalism" title="Circassian nationalism">Circassian</a> slave. Entitled, 'Vornehmner Kaufmann mit seinem cirkassischen Sklaven' [Distinguished merchant and his circassian slave] by <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Snouck_Hurgronje" title="Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje">Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje</a>, ca. 1888.</div></div></div>
<p>Between the late 18th and early-to-mid-19th centuries, the Adyghe people lost their independence as the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> gradually carried out a series of wars and campaigns. During this period, the Adyghe plight achieved a certain celebrity status in the West; but pledges of assistance were never fulfilled. After the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1853 to 1856, Russia turned its attention to the Caucasus in earnest. Following major territorial losses for <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%931813)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–1813)">Russo-Persian War (1804–1813)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%931828)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826–1828)">Russo-Persian War (1826–1828)</a>, forcing Persia to cede what comprises now <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> to Imperial Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russia found itself able to focus most of its army on subduing the rebelling natives of the North Caucasus, starting with the peoples of <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechnya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>. In 1859 the Russians finished defeating <a href="/wiki/Imam_Shamil" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Shamil">Imam Shamil</a> in the eastern Caucasus, and turned their attention westward. Eventually, the long-lasting <a href="/wiki/Russian%E2%80%93Circassian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian–Circassian War">Russian–Circassian War</a>, which had begun a hundred years earlier, ended with the defeat of the Adyghe forces. Some Adyghe leaders signed loyalty oaths on 2 June 1864 (21 May, <a href="/wiki/Old_Style" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Style">O.S.</a>).
</p><p>
The conquest of the Caucasus by the Russian Empire in the 19th century during the Russian-Circassian War led to the destruction and killing of many Adyghe—towards the end of the conflict, the Russian General <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nikolai_Yevdokimov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nikolai Yevdokimov (page does not exist)">Nikolai Yevdokimov</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%95%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%B2,_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B9_%D0%98%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" class="extiw" title="ru:Евдокимов, Николай Иванович">ru</a>&#93;</span> had the task of driving the remaining Circassian inhabitants out of the region, primarily into the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Mobile columns of Russian riflemen and <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossack</a> cavalry carried out the task.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_n_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_n-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_o_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_o-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-King_2008:_94–96_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King_2008:_94–96-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> </p><blockquote><p>"In a series of sweeping military campaigns lasting from 1860 to 1864... the northwest Caucasus and the Black Sea coast were virtually emptied of Muslim villagers. Columns of the displaced were marched either to the Kuban [River] plains or toward the coast for transport to the Ottoman Empire... One after another, entire Circassian tribal groups were dispersed, resettled, or killed en masse"<sup id="cite_ref-King_2008:_94–96_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King_2008:_94–96-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p> In 1840 <a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich_Neumann" title="Karl Friedrich Neumann">Karl Friedrich Neumann</a> estimated the Circassian casualties at around one and a half million.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_q_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_q-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Some sources state that hundreds of thousands of others died during the exodus.<sup id="cite_ref-Shenfield_1999_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shenfield_1999-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Several historians use the phrase "Circassian massacres"<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_r_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_r-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> for the consequences of Russian actions in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_s_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_s-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Like other ethnic minorities under Russian rule, the Adyghe who remained in the Russian Empire borders were subjected to policies of mass resettlement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>It has been estimated that the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, which ruled large parts of the area south of Russia, imported some 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">slaves</a>—mainly Circassians—between 1800 and 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman Empire regarded the Adyghe warriors as courageous and well-experienced. It encouraged them to settle in various near-border settlements of the Ottoman Empire in order to strengthen the empire's borders.
</p><p>According to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Walter_Richmond&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Walter Richmond (page does not exist)">Walter Richmond</a>,
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Circassia was a small independent nation on the northeastern shore of the Black Sea. For no reason other than ethnic hatred, over the course of hundreds of raids the Russians drove the Circassians from their homeland and deported them to the Ottoman Empire. At least 600,000 people lost their lives to massacre, starvation, and the elements while hundreds of thousands more were forced to leave their homeland. By 1864, three-fourths of the population was annihilated, and the Circassians had become one of the first stateless peoples in modern history".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-exile_period">Post-exile period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Post-exile period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Adyghe whom the Ottomans settled in various near-border settlements across the Ottoman Empire ended up living across many territories in the Middle East. At the time these lands belonged to the Ottoman Empire; now Adyghes have established communities in the following countries:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Turkey" title="Circassians in Turkey">Turkey</a>, which has the largest Adyghe population in the world. The Adyghe settled in three main regions in Turkey: <a href="/wiki/Samsun" title="Samsun">Samsun</a>, along the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>; the region near the city of <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>, the region near the city of <a href="/wiki/Kayseri" title="Kayseri">Kayseri</a>, and in the western part of the country near the region of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. This latter region experienced a <a href="/wiki/1999_%C4%B0zmit_earthquake" title="1999 İzmit earthquake">severe earthquake in 1999</a>. Many Adyghe played key roles in the Ottoman army and also participated in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> of 1919–1923.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Syria" title="Circassians in Syria">Syria</a> – Most of the Adyghe who immigrated to Syria settled in the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> of 1967, the Adyghe people – then estimated at 30,000 in number – were the majority group in the Golan Heights region. The most prominent settlement in the Golan was the town of <a href="/wiki/Quneitra" title="Quneitra">Quneitra</a>. The total number of Circassians in Syria is estimated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (June 2019)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> at between 50,000 and 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, as tensions between the <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athism" title="Ba&#39;athism">Baath government</a> and the opposition forces escalated, Syrian Circassians said they were exploring returning to Circassia. Circassians from different parts of Syria, such as <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>, have moved back to the Golan Heights, believed to be safer. Some refugees have been reportedly killed by shelling. Circassians have lobbied the Russian and Israeli governments to help evacuate refugees from Syria; Russia has issued some visas.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Israel" title="Circassians in Israel">Israel</a> – The Adyghe initially settled in three places—in <a href="/wiki/Kfar_Kama" title="Kfar Kama">Kfar Kama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rehaniya" title="Rehaniya">Rehaniya</a>, and in the region of <a href="/wiki/Hadera" title="Hadera">Hadera</a>. Due to a <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> epidemic, the Adyghe eventually abandoned the settlement near Hadera. Though Sunni Muslim, Adyghe within Israel are seen as a loyal minority who serve in the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israeli armed forces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_Jordan_13_February_2007-9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Circassian Guards in Jordan</div></div></div></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> – The Adyghe had a major role in the history of the Kingdom of Jordan.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Over the years, various Adyghe have served in distinguished roles in the kingdom of Jordan. Adyghes have served as a prime minister (<a href="/wiki/Sa%27id_al-Mufti" class="mw-redirect" title="Sa&#39;id al-Mufti">Sa'id al-Mufti</a>), as ministers (commonly at least one minister should represent the Circassians in each cabinet), as high-ranking officers, etc., and due to their important role in the history of Jordan, Adyghe form the <a href="/wiki/Hashemites" title="Hashemites">Hashemites</a>' <a href="/wiki/Honour_guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Honour guard">honour guard</a> at the royal palaces. They represented Jordan in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Edinburgh_Military_Tattoo" title="Royal Edinburgh Military Tattoo">Royal Edinburgh Military Tattoo</a> in 2010, joining other honour guards such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Airborne_Ceremonial_Unit&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Airborne Ceremonial Unit (page does not exist)">Airborne Ceremonial Unit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Jordanian Circassians cluster around several areas, most notably <a href="/wiki/Sweileh" title="Sweileh">Sweileh</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amman" title="Amman">Amman</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iraq" title="Circassians in Iraq">Iraq</a> – Adyghe came to <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> directly from <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">Circassia</a>. They settled in all parts of Iraq—from north to south—but most of all in Iraq's capital <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. Many Adyghe also settled in <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">Kerkuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diyala_Governorate" title="Diyala Governorate">Diyala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>, and other places. Circassians have played major roles in different periods throughout Iraq's history, and made great contributions to political and military institutions in the country, to the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Army" title="Iraqi Army">Iraqi Army</a> in particular. Several Iraqi prime ministers have been of Circassian descent.</li></ul>
<p>The actions of the Russian military in acquiring Circassian land through expulsion and massacres<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_p_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_p-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> have given rise to a movement among descendants of the expelled ethnicities for international recognition of the perpetration of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNPO_2006._75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPO_2006.-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> 
On 20 May 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> parliament voted in a 95 to 0 declaration that Russia had committed genocide when it engaged in massacres against Circassians in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg/190px-Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg/285px-Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg/380px-Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="757" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beslan_Mudranov_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian-Circassian wrestler <a href="/wiki/Beslan_Mudranov" title="Beslan Mudranov">Beslan Mudranov</a> won Russia's first gold medal at the Rio 2016 Olympics</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Circassian_music" title="Circassian music">Circassian music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Circassian_folklore" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian folklore">Circassian folklore</a></div>
<p>Adyghe society prior to the Russian invasion was highly stratified. While a few princedoms in the mountainous regions of Adygeya were fairly egalitarian, most were broken into strict <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">castes</a>. The highest was the caste of the "princes", followed by a caste of lesser nobility, and then commoners, serfs, and slaves. In the decades before Russian rule, two princedoms overthrew their traditional rulers and set up democratic processes, but this social experiment was cut short by the end of Adyghe independence.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CircassianFamilyTree.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/CircassianFamilyTree.png/220px-CircassianFamilyTree.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/CircassianFamilyTree.png/330px-CircassianFamilyTree.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/CircassianFamilyTree.png/440px-CircassianFamilyTree.png 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CircassianFamilyTree.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Circassian dialects and sub-dialects development</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG/220px-Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG/330px-Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG/440px-Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="325" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwest_Caucasian_Family_Tree.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The isolated Northwest Caucasian language family</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe language</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kabardian_language" title="Kabardian language">Kabardian language</a></div>
<p>Circassians mainly speak the <a href="/wiki/Circassian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian language">Circassian language</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages" title="Northwest Caucasian languages">Northwest Caucasian language</a> with numerous dialects, the primary ones being <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a> (West Circassian) and <a href="/wiki/Kabardian_language" title="Kabardian language">Kabardian</a> (East Adyghe). West Adyghe language is based on Temirgoy (Chemirgoy) dialect, while East Adyghe language is based on Kabardian dialect. Circassians also speak <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> in large numbers, having been <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiled</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> to lands of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, where the majority of them live today, and some to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>, to which they came primarily through mass deportations by the <a href="/wiki/Safavids" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavids">Safavids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qajars" class="mw-redirect" title="Qajars">Qajars</a> or, to a lesser extent, as <a href="/wiki/Muhacir" title="Muhacir">muhajirs</a> in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Linguists divide the Northwest Caucasian languages into Circassian (including Kabardian), Ubykh (originally an Circassian dialect, theorised to be the original form of Circassian language), and <a href="/wiki/Abazgi_languages" title="Abazgi languages">Abazgi (Abkhaz-Abaza)</a>. Ubykh and Circassian are practically the same language. The Ubykhs lived on the Black Sea coast, around the city of Sochi, the capital of Circassia, north of Abkhazia.
</p><p>Although related, Abazgi and Circassian are mutually unintelligible. Abazgi is spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Abkhazians" title="Abkhazians">Abkhazians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abazins" title="Abazins">Abazins</a>.The Abkhazians lived on the coast between the Circassians and the Georgians, were organized as the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Abkhazia" title="Principality of Abkhazia">Principality of Abkhazia</a> and were involved with the Georgians to some degree. The Abazins or Abaza, their relatives, lived north of the mountains and were involved with Circassia proper. They extended from the mountain crest northeast onto the steppe and partially separated the Kabardians from the rest. <a href="/wiki/Sadz" title="Sadz">Sadz</a> were either northern Abkhazian or eastern Abaza, depending on the source.
</p><p>Walter Richmond writes that the Circassian language in Russia is "gravely threatened." He argues that Russian policy of surrounding small Circassian communities with Slavic populations has created conditions where Circassian language and nationality will disappear. By the 1990s, Russian had become the standard language for business in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Adygea" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Adygea">Republic of Adygea</a>, even within communities with Circassian majority populations.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_Habze" title="Adyghe Habze">Adyghe Habze</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg/220px-Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg/330px-Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg/440px-Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Darweesh_Mosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> of Abu Darwish (Adyghe descendant), one of the oldest mosques in <a href="/wiki/Amman" title="Amman">Amman</a> and considered as a major <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">landmark</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Ancestors of modern Adyghe people gradually went through following various religions: <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">Monotheism</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, and then Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is the tradition of the early church that Christianity made its first appearance in Circassia in the first century AD via the travels and preaching of the <a href="/wiki/Andrew_the_Apostle" title="Andrew the Apostle">Apostle Andrew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated95_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated95-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> spread throughout the Caucasus between the 4th century<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the 6th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ab_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ab-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A small Muslim presence in Circassia has existed since the Middle Ages, but widespread Islamization occurred after 1717, when Sultan Murad IV ordered the Crimean Khans to spread Islam among the Circassians, with the Ottomans and Crimeans seeing some success in converting members of the aristocracy who would then ultimately spread the religion to their dependents.<sup id="cite_ref-NathoIslamization_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NathoIslamization-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> However, despite the efforts of the Ottomans and their Crimean and Circassian clients, the masses of the Circassian people remained Christian and pagan, until the threat of Russian conquest impelled the majority of them to convert in order to cement defensive alliances with the Ottoman Empire and the Crimean Khanate to protect their independence.<sup id="cite_ref-NathoIslamization_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NathoIslamization-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Significant Christian and pagan presence remained among some tribes such as the Shapsugs and Natukhai with Islamization pressures implemented by those loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Emirate" title="Caucasus Emirate">Caucasus Emirate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Sufi orders including the <a href="/wiki/Qadiri" class="mw-redirect" title="Qadiri">Qadiri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nakshbandi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nakshbandi">Nakshbandi</a> orders gained prominence and played a role in spreading Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, a large majority of Circassians remain Muslim, with minorities of atheists<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-Bram_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bram-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Atheist Circassians tend to be of the younger generation (20–35 years old), in which they were found to constitute a quarter of Circassians in Kabardino-Balkaria.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Among Christians, Catholicism, originally introduced along the coasts by Venetian and Genoese traders, today constitutes just under 1% of Kabardins.<sup id="cite_ref-Sreda_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sreda-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Some Circassians are also Orthodox Christian, notably including those in <a href="/wiki/Mozdok" title="Mozdok">Mozdok</a><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and some of those <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kursky_district&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kursky district (page does not exist)">Kursky district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenwood_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenwood-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Among Muslims, Islamic observance varies widely between those who only know a few prayers with a Muslim identity that is more "cultural" than religious, to those who regularly observe all requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both Islam and the Habze are identified as national characteristics even by those that do not practice.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyugasheva_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyugasheva-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Today, Islam is a central part of life in many Circassian diaspora communities, such as in Israel, while in the Circassian homeland Soviet rule saw an extensive process of <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularization</a>, and there is wide influence of many social norms which contradict Islamic law, such as widespread observance of traditional pre-Islamic moral codes contradicting those of Islam, and norms like social alcohol consumption; in Israel, meanwhile, such non-Islamic social norms are not present.<sup id="cite_ref-Bram_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bram-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the modern times, it has been reported that those who identify primarily as adherents of the native Habze faith (as opposed to another listed faith) constitute 12% of the population of Karachay-Cherkessia and 3% of the population of Kabardino-Balkaria.<sup id="cite_ref-ArenaAtlas_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArenaAtlas-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2012maps_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012maps-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> There have also been reports of violence and threats against those "reviving" and diffusing the original Circassian pre-Islamic faith.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The relationship between <i>habze</i> and Islam varies between Circassian communities; for some, there is conflict between the two, while for others, such as in Israel, they are seen as complementary philosophies.<sup id="cite_ref-Bram_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bram-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_social_system">Traditional social system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditional social system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USSHER(1865)_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg/250px-USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg/375px-USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg/500px-USSHER%281865%29_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2063" data-file-height="1463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USSHER(1865)_p183_CIRCASSIAN_DANCE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Circassian dance</div></div></div>
<p>Society was organized by <i>Adyghe khabze</i>, or Circassian custom.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Many of these customs had equivalents throughout the mountains. The seemingly disorganized Circassians resisted the Russians just as effectively as the organized theocracy of <a href="/wiki/Imam_Shamil" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Shamil">Imam Shamil</a>. The aristocracy was called <i>warq</i>. Some aristocratic families held the rank of <i>Pshi</i> or prince and the eldest member of this family was the <i>Pshi-tkhamade</i> who was the tribal chief. Below the warq was the large class to <i>tfokotl</i>, roughly yeomen or freemen, who had various duties to the warq.
</p><p>They were divided into clans of some sort. Below them were three classes approximating serfs or slaves. Of course, these Circassian social terms do not exactly match their European equivalents. Since everything was a matter custom, much depended on time, place, circumstances and personality. The three 'democratic' princedoms, Natukhai, Shapsug, and Abdzakh, managed their affairs by assemblies called <i>Khase</i> or larger ones called <i>Zafes</i>.
</p><p>Decisions were made by general agreement and there was no formal mechanism to enforce decisions. The democratic princedoms, who were perhaps the majority, lived mainly in the mountains where they were relatively protected from the Russians. They seem to have retained their aristocrats, but with diminished powers. In the remaining 'feudal' princedoms power was theoretically in the hands of the <i>Pshi-tkhamade</i>, although his power could be limited by Khases or other influential families.
</p><p>In addition to the vertical relations of class there were many horizontal relations between unrelated persons. There was a strong tradition of hospitality similar to the Greek <a href="/wiki/Xenia_(Greek)" title="Xenia (Greek)">xenia</a>. Many houses would have a <i>kunakskaya</i> or guest room. The duty of a host extended even to <i>abreks</i> or outlaws. Two men might be sworn brothers or <i>kunaks</i>. There were brotherhoods of unrelated individuals called <i>tleuzh</i> who provided each other mutual support. It was common for a child to be raised by an <i>atalyk</i> or foster father. Criminal law was mainly concerned with reconciling the two parties. Adyghe khabze is sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Adat" title="Adat">adat</a> when it is contrasted to the kind of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic law">Islamic law</a> advocated by people like <a href="/wiki/Imam_Shamil" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Shamil">Imam Shamil</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_clothing">Traditional clothing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Traditional clothing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_clothing,_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG/300px-Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG/450px-Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG/600px-Traditional_clothing%2C_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_clothing,_Circassian_Heritage_Center.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Circassian clothing</div></div></div>
<p>The traditional female clothing (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Бзылъфыгъэ Шъуашэр, Bzıłfıǵe Ȿuaşer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[bzəɬfəʁa ʂʷaːʃar]</a></span>) was very diverse and highly decorated and mainly depends on the region, class of family, occasions, and princedoms. The traditional female costume is composed of a dress (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Джанэр, Janer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[d͡ʒaːnar]</a></span>), coat (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Сае, Saye</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[saːja]</a></span>), shirt, pant (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">ДжэнэкӀакор, Jeneç'akuer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[d͡ʒanat͡ʃʼaːkʷar]</a></span>), vest (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">КӀэкӀ, Ç'eç'</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[t͡ʃʼat͡ʃʼ]</a></span>), lamb leather bra (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Шъохътан, Ȿuex́tan</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ʂʷaχtaːn]</a></span>), a variety of hats ({{lang-ady |ПэӀохэр}, Peꜧuexer} <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[paʔʷaxar]</a></span>), shoes, and belts (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Бгырыпхыхэр, Bğırıpxıxer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[bɣərəpxəxar]</a></span>).
</p><p>Holiday dresses are made of expensive fabrics such as <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Velvet" title="Velvet">velvet</a>. The traditional colors of women's clothing rarely includes blue, green or bright-colored tones, instead mostly white, red, black and brown shades are worn. The Circassian dresses were embroidered with gold and silver threads. These embroideries were handmade and took time to complete as they were very intricate.
</p><p>The traditional male costume (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Адыгэ хъулъфыгъэ шъуашэр, Adığe X́uıłfıǵe Ȿuaşer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[aːdəɣa χʷəɬfəʁa ʂʷaːʃar]</a></span>) includes a coat with wide sleeves, shirt, pants, a dagger, sword, and a variety of hats and shoes. Traditionally, young men in the warriors times wore coat with short sleeves—in order to feel more comfortable in combat. Different colors of clothing for males were strictly used to distinguish between different social classes, for example white is usually worn by princes, red by nobles, gray, brown, and black by peasants (blue, green and the other colors were rarely worn).
</p><p>A compulsory item in the traditional male costume is a dagger and a sword. The traditional Adyghean sword is called <a href="/wiki/Shashka" title="Shashka">Shashka</a>. It is a special kind of <a href="/wiki/Sabre" title="Sabre">sabre</a>; a very sharp, single-edged, single-handed, and <a href="/wiki/Hilt" title="Hilt">guardless</a> <a href="/wiki/Sword" title="Sword">sword</a>. Although the sword is used by most of Russian and Ukrainian Cossacks, the typically Adyghean form of the sabre is longer than the Cossack type, and in fact the word Shashka came from the Adyghe word "Sashkhwa" (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">Сашьхъуэ, Sas̨x́ue</span>) which means "long knife". On the breast of the costume are long ornamental tubes or sticks, once filled with a single charge of gunpowder (called gaziri cartridges) and used to reload muskets.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_cuisine">Traditional cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Traditional cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg/220px-Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg/330px-Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg/440px-Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Circassian_traditional_house.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An old country house and traditional cuisine with <a href="/wiki/Haliva" title="Haliva">Haliva</a> (Хьэлжъо, Helɀwa) and <a href="/wiki/Mataz" title="Mataz">Mataz</a> (Мэтазэ, Metaze), two of the prominent traditional Adyghe snacks.</div></div></div>
<p>The Adyghe <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisine</a> is rich with different dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ac_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ac-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In the summer, the traditional dishes consumed by the Adyghe people are mainly <a href="/wiki/Dairy_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Dairy products">dairy products</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetable</a> dishes. In the winter and spring the traditional dishes are mainly <a href="/wiki/Flour" title="Flour">flour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a> dishes. An example of the latter is known as <a href="/wiki/Ficcin" class="mw-redirect" title="Ficcin">ficcin</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Circassian_cheese" title="Circassian cheese">Circassian cheese</a> is considered one of the more famous types of cheeses in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>.
</p><p>A popular traditional dish is <a href="/wiki/Chicken_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicken (food)">chicken</a> or <a href="/wiki/Turkey_as_food" title="Turkey as food">turkey</a> with sauce, seasoned with crushed garlic and red pepper. <a href="/wiki/Mutton" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutton">Mutton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a> are served boiled, usually with a seasoning of sour <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> with crushed garlic and salt.
</p><p>Variants of pasta are found. A type of <a href="/wiki/Ravioli" title="Ravioli">ravioli</a> may be encountered, which is filled with potato or beef.
</p><p>On holidays the Adyghe people traditionally make <a href="/wiki/Haliva" title="Haliva">Haliva</a> (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">хьэлжъо, Helɀua</span>) (fried triangular pastries with mainly Circassian cheese or potato), from toasted millet or wheat flour in syrup, baked cakes and pies. In the Levant there is a famous Circassian dish which is called Tajen Alsharkaseiah.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_crafts">Traditional crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Traditional crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Adyghes have been famous for making <a href="/wiki/Carpets" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpets">carpets</a> (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">пӏуаблэхэр, P'uablexer</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[pʷʼaːblaxar]</a></span>) or mats worldwide for thousands of years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Making carpets was very hard work in which collecting raw materials is restricted to a specific period within the year. The raw materials were dried, and based on the intended colours, different methods of drying were applied. For example, when dried in the shade, its<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> colour changed to a beautiful light gold colour. If it were dried in direct sun light then it would have a silver colour, and if they wanted to have a dark colour for the carpets, the raw materials were put in a pool of water and covered by <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">poplar</a> leaves (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">екӏэпцӏэ, Yeç'epc'e</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[jat͡ʃʼapt͡sʼa]</a></span>).
</p><p>The carpets were adorned with images of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>, beloved <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> (<a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a>), and plants, and the image of the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> was widely used.
</p><p>The carpets were used for different reasons due to their characteristic resistance to <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a> and cold, and in retaining heat. Also, there was a tradition in Circassian homes to have two carpets hanging in the guest room, one used to hang over <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">шхончымрэ, Şxuençımre</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ʃxʷant͡ʃəmra]</a></span>) and pistols (<a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">Adyghe</a>: <span lang="ady">къэлаеымрэ, Qelayeımre</span>), and the other used to hang over musical instruments.
</p><p>The carpets were used to pray upon, and it was necessary for every Circassian girl to make three carpets before <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a>; a big carpet, a small carpet, and the last for praying as a <a href="/wiki/Prayer_rug" title="Prayer rug">prayer rug</a>. These carpets would give the grooms an impression as to the success of their brides in their homes after marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ad_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ad-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tribes">Tribes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tribes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From the <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">late Middle Ages</a>, a number of territorial- and political-based Circassian tribes or ethnic entities began to take shape. They had slightly different dialects.
</p><p>Dialects came to exist after Circassia was divided into princedoms (tribes) after the death of King Yinal of Circassia, who united Circassia for the last time before its short reunion during the Russo-Caucasian War. As the logistics between the princedoms became harder, each princedom became slightly isolated from one another, thus the people living under the banner of each princedom developed their own dialects. In time, the dialects they speak were named after their princedoms. After a longer while, the people began being called after the princedom which they live under the banner of. Therefore, there is a widespread misconception of these princedoms actually being tribes. Opposed to that, the notion "tribe" is non-existent in the Circassian culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_War" title="Caucasian War">Caucasian War</a> most Circassians were expelled to the Ottoman Empire, and many of the princedoms were destroyed and the people evicted from their historical homeland in 1864.
</p><p>The main groups within the Circassian people are the <a href="/wiki/Adygeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Adygeans">Adygeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abzakh_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abzakh people">Abzakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cherkess" title="Cherkess">Cherkess</a>. This does not include tribal subgroups.
</p><p>Most Adyghe living in <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">Circassia</a> are Bzhedug, Kabardian, and Temirgoy, while the majority in <a href="/wiki/Circassian_diaspora" title="Circassian diaspora">diaspora</a> are Kabardian, Abdzakh, and Shapsug. West Adyghe language is based on Temirgoy dialect, while East Adyghe language is based on Kabardian dialect.
</p><p>The twelve stars on the Circassian flag symbolize the individual tribes of the Circassians; the nine stars within the arc symbolize the nine aristocratic tribes of Adygea, and the three horizontal stars symbolize the three democratic tribes. The twelve tribes are the Abdzakh, Besleney, Bzhedug, Hatuqwai, Kabardian, Mamkhegh, Natukhai, Shapsug, Temirgoy, Ubykh, Yegeruqwai, and Zhaney.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td><i>Махошъ, Mexuaȿ</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[maːxʷaʂ]</a></span>
</td>
<td>A large clan, but not enough to be a separate tribe
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Circassian tribes can be grouped and compared in various ways. The Kabarda occupied about a third of the north Caucasus piedmont from east of Circassia proper eastward to the Chechen country. To their north were the Nogai nomads and to the south, deeper in the mountains, were from west to east, the Karachays, Balkars, Ossetes, Ingushes, and Chechens. The Kabardians were fairly advanced, interacted with the Russians from the sixteenth century and were much reduced by plague in the early nineteenth century.
</p>

style="position:absolute;top:61.5%;left:34.167%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Gelendzhik-"
