style="position:absolute;top:72%;left:51.167%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Tuapse-----" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/8px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Tuapse-----" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/12px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/16px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right">Tuapse-----</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:85.5%;left:62.167%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Sochi-----" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/8px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Sochi-----" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/12px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/16px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right">Sochi-----</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:91.75%;left:70.333%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Gagra-----" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/8px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Gagra-----" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/12px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Location_dot_clear.svg/16px-Location_dot_clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right">Gagra-----</div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Relief_Map_of_Krasnodarski_Krai.png" title="File:Relief Map of Krasnodarski Krai.png"> </a></div>Approximate location of Circassian princedoms, Tsutsiev's Atlas</div></div></div>
<p>As for the Circassians proper, apparently called Kiakhs, some writers speak of twelve princedoms and some do not.
</p>
<ul><li>The narrow <b>Black Sea coast</b> was occupied, from north to south by the <a href="/wiki/Natukhai" class="mw-redirect" title="Natukhai">Natukhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shapsug" class="mw-redirect" title="Shapsug">Shapsug</a>, Ubykh, and the Abkhaz (<a href="/wiki/Sadz" title="Sadz">Sadz</a> sub-branch). The main part of the Natukhai and Shapsug princedoms located in north of the mountains. The Natukhai were enriched by trade since their coast was not backed by high mountains and opened onto the steppe.</li>
<li>The <b>north slope</b> was inhabited, from north to south, by the Natukhai, Shapsug, Abdzakh, and Abaza. They seem to have been the most populous princedoms after the Kabarda and its inland location gave then some protection from Nogai and Cossack raiding.</li>
<li>In the <b>far west</b> were three small princedoms that were absorbed into the Natukhai and disappeared. These were the Adele <a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5" class="extiw" title="ru:Адале">ru:Адале</a> on the Taman peninsula and the Shegak and Chebsin (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A5%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BA%D0%B8" class="extiw" title="ru:Хегайки">ru:Хегайки</a> and <a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%BD" class="extiw" title="ru:Чебсин">ru:Чебсин</a>) near Anapa.</li>
<li>Along the <b>Kuban</b> were the Natukhai, Zhaney, Bzhedug, Hatuqwai, and Temirgoy.</li>
<li>On the <b>east</b>, between the Laba and Belaya, from north to south, were the Temirgoy, Yegeruqwai (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D1%86%D1%8B" class="extiw" title="ru:Егерукаевцы">ru:Егерукаевцы</a>), Makhosh (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%85%D0%BE%D1%88%D0%B5%D0%B2%D1%86%D1%8B" class="extiw" title="ru:Махошевцы">ru:Махошевцы</a>), <a href="/wiki/Besleney" title="Besleney">Besleney</a> and Abaza. The Besleney were a branch of the Kabardians. The Tapanta (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0" class="extiw" title="ru:Тапанта">ru:Тапанта</a>), a branch of the Abaza, lived between the Besleney and Kabardian princedoms on the upper Kuban. Along the Belaya River were the Temirgoy, the ill-documented Ademey (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%86%D1%8B" class="extiw" title="ru:Адамийцы">ru:Адамийцы</a>) and then the <a href="/wiki/Mamkhegh" title="Mamkhegh">Mamkhegh</a> near the modern <a href="/wiki/Maykop" title="Maykop">Maykop</a>.</li>
<li>The Guaye (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%93%D1%83%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%B5" class="extiw" title="ru:Гуайе">ru:Гуайе</a>) are poorly documented. The Tchelugay lived west of the Makhosh. The Hakuch lived on the coast south of the Natukhai. Other groups are mentioned without much documentation. There are reports of princedoms migrating from one place to another, again without much documentation. Some sketch maps show a group of <a href="/wiki/Karachays" title="Karachays">Karachays</a> on the upper Laba without any explanation.</li></ul>
<p>The princedoms along the Kuban and Laba rivers were exposed to Nogai and Cossack raiding while those in the interior had some protection. The three "democratic" princedoms were the Natukhai, Shapsug, and Abdzakh. They managed their affairs by assemblies while the other princedoms were controlled by "princes" or <i>Pshi</i>. Princedoms with remnants in the Caucasus are: Kabarda (the largest), the Temirgoy and Bzhedug in Adygea, and the Shapsug near Tuapse and to the north of Tuapsiysiy Rayon of Krasnodarskiy Kray. There are also a few Besleney and Natukhai villages, and an Abdzakh village.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Circassian_diaspora">Circassian diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Circassian diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Circassian_diaspora" title="Circassian diaspora">Circassian diaspora</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg/220px-Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg/330px-Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg/440px-Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3821" data-file-height="1810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Circassian_horsemanship_during_Sir_Herbert_Samuel%27s_second_visit_to_Transjordan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adyghe <a href="/wiki/Horsemanship" class="mw-redirect" title="Horsemanship">horsemanship</a> in <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>, April 1921</div></div></div>
<p>Much of Adyghe culture was disrupted after the conquest of <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">their homeland</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> in 1864. The Circassian people were subjected to <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic cleansing of Circassians">ethnic cleansing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">mass exile</a> mainly to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Qajar_Iran" title="Qajar Iran">Qajar Iran</a> and the Balkans. This increased the number of Circassians in the region and even created several entirely new Circassian communities in the states that got created after the dissolution of the Ottoman Empire. However, Adyghe have also lived outside the Caucasus region since the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. They were particularly well represented in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Egypt</a>.
</p><p>The total number of Circassians worldwide is estimated at 8 million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Turkey" title="Circassians in Turkey">Circassians in Turkey</a></div>
<p>Around half of all Circassians live in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, mainly in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Samsun_Province" title="Samsun Province">Samsun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ordu_Province" title="Ordu Province">Ordu</a> (in Northern Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Kahramanmara%C5%9F_Province" title="Kahramanmaraş Province">Kahramanmaraş</a> (in Southern Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Kayseri_Province" title="Kayseri Province">Kayseri</a> (in Central Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Band%C4%B1rma" title="Bandırma">Bandırma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCzce_Province" title="Düzce Province">Düzce</a> (in Northwest Turkey).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tumanbay_II_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tumanbay_II_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Tumanbay_II_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d5/Tumanbay_II_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="233" data-file-height="304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tumanbay_II_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tuman_bay_II" title="Tuman bay II">Tuman bay II</a> (reigned 1516–1517) the last Mamluk sultan of Adyghe origins</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Egypt" title="Circassians in Egypt">Circassians in Egypt</a></div>
<p>During the 13th century the Mamluks seized power in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. Some 15th-century Circassian converts to Islam became <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a> and rose through the ranks of the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluk dynasty</a> to high positions, some becoming sultans in Egypt such as <a href="/wiki/Qaitbay" title="Qaitbay">Qaitbay</a>, Mamluk Sultan of Egypt (1468–1496). The majority of the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Burji_dynasty" title="Burji dynasty">Burji Mamluk dynasty</a> in Egypt (1382–1517) had Circassian origins,<sup id="cite_ref-GPG_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPG-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> while also including Abkhaz, Abaza, and Georgian peoples whom the Arab sultans had recruited to serve their kingdoms as a military force. With the rise of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhammad Ali Pasha">Muhammad Ali Pasha</a> (who ruled Egypt from 1805 to 1848), most senior Mamluks were killed by him in order to secure his rule and the remaining Mamluks fled to <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Most Circassian communities in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> were assimilated into the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> several thousand Adyghe reside in Egypt; in addition to the descendants of Burji Mamluks of Adyghe origin, there are many who descend from royal Circassian consorts or Ottoman pashas of Circassian origin as well as Circassian <a href="/wiki/Muhajirun" title="Muhajirun">muhajirs</a> of the 19th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iran" title="Circassians in Iran">Circassians in Iran</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> has a significant Circassian population.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> It once had a very large community, but the vast amount were assimilated in the population in the course of centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Safavid" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavid">Safavid</a> (1501–1736) and <a href="/wiki/Qajar" class="mw-redirect" title="Qajar">Qajar</a> (1789–1925) dynasties saw the importing and deporting of large numbers of Circassians to <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>, where many enjoyed prestige in the <a href="/wiki/Harems" class="mw-redirect" title="Harems">harems</a> and in the élite armies (the so-called <i>ghulams</i>), while many others settled and deployed as craftsmen, labourers, farmers and regular soldiers. Many members of the Safavid nobility and élite had Circassian ancestry and Circassian dignitaries, such as the kings <a href="/wiki/Abbas_II_of_Persia" title="Abbas II of Persia">Abbas II of Persia</a> (reigned 1642–1666) and <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_I_of_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Suleiman I of Persia">Suleiman I of Persia</a> (reigned 1666–1694). While traces of Circassian settlements in Iran have lasted into the 20th century, many of the once large Circassian minority became assimilated into the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
However, significant communities of Circassians continue to live in particular cities in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> like Tabriz and Tehran, and in the northern provinces of <a href="/wiki/Gilan" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilan">Gilan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazandaran" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazandaran">Mazandaran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WaldmanMason2006_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaldmanMason2006-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Notable places of traditional Circassian settlement in Iran include <a href="/wiki/Gilan_Province" title="Gilan Province">Gilan Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fars_Province" title="Fars Province">Fars Province</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">Isfahan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> (due to contemporary migration). <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iran" title="Circassians in Iran">Circassians in Iran</a> are the nation's second largest Caucasus-derived nation after the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Georgians" title="Iranian Georgians">Georgians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rest_of_Western_Asia">Rest of Western Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rest of Western Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Significant communities live in <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LLOW_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LLOW-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Syria" title="Circassians in Syria">Circassians in Syria</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-LLOW_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LLOW-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and smaller communities live in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> (in the villages of <a href="/wiki/Kfar_Kama" title="Kfar Kama">Kfar Kama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rehaniya" title="Rehaniya">Rehaniya</a>—see <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Israel" title="Circassians in Israel">Circassians in Israel</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-LLOW_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LLOW-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Circassians are also present <a href="/wiki/Circassians_in_Iraq" title="Circassians in Iraq">in Iraq</a>. <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah" title="Sulaymaniyah">Sulaymaniyah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diyala_Governorate" title="Diyala Governorate">Diyala</a> comprise the country's main cities with Circassians,<sup id="cite_ref-ORSAM_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ORSAM-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> though lesser numbers are spread in other regions and cities as well.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg/220px-Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg/330px-Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg/440px-Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2226" data-file-height="1369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clash_with_Cherkessians.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Serbian troops clashing with Circassians during the <a href="/wiki/Serbian-Turkish_Wars_(1876-1878)" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian-Turkish Wars (1876-1878)">Serbian-Turkish War</a>, 1876–1878</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rest_of_Europe">Rest of Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Rest of Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Out of 1,010 Circassians living in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (473 <a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardian Adyghe</a> (Kabardin),<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> 338 <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_people" title="Adyghe people">Adygean Adyghe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and 190 <a href="/wiki/Cherkesses" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherkesses">Cherkessian Adyghe</a> (Cherkess)<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>—after the existing <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> division of Circassians into three groups), only 181 (17.9%) declared fluency in the native language; 96 (9.5%) declared <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> as their native language, and 697 (69%) marked "other language" as being their native language. The major Adyghe community in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>.
</p><p>There is a small community of Circassians in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>. A number of Adyghe also settled in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> in 1864–1865 but most fled after it became separate from the Ottoman Empire in 1878. The small community that settled in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Adyghes" title="Kosovo Adyghes">Kosovo Adyghes</a>) repatriated to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Adygea" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Adygea">Republic of Adygea</a> in 1998.
</p><p>There are Circassians in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and a small number in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Numerous Circassians have also immigrated to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and settled in <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>. There is also a small Circassian community in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sochi_Olympics_controversy">Sochi Olympics controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circassians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sochi Olympics controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg/220px-%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg/330px-%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg/440px-%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="475" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%87erkez_s%C3%BCrg%C3%BCn%C3%BCn%C3%BCn_an%C4%B1lmas%C4%B1_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Circassians commemorate the banishment of the Circassians from Russia in <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="İstanbul">İstanbul</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Concerns_and_controversies_at_the_2014_Winter_Olympics" title="Concerns and controversies at the 2014 Winter Olympics">Concerns and controversies at the 2014 Winter Olympics</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a> facilities in <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a> (once the Circassian capital)<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> were built in areas that were claimed to contain <a href="/wiki/Mass_grave" title="Mass grave">mass graves</a> of Circassians who were killed during <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> in military campaigns lasting from 1860 to 1864.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Adyghe organizations in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and the Adyghe diaspora around the world requested that construction at the site stop and that the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> not be held at the site of the <a href="/wiki/Circassian_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Circassian Genocide">Adyghe genocide</a>, to prevent desecration of Adyghe graves. According to Iyad Youghar, who headed the lobby group <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Circassian_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Circassian Council (page does not exist)">International Circassian Council</a>: "We want the athletes to know that if they compete here they will be skiing on the bones of our relatives."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The year 2014 also marked the 150th anniversary of the Circassian Genocide which angered the Circassians around the world. Many protests were held all over the world to stop the Sochi Olympics, but were not successful.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-The_Formation_of_a_Circassian_Diaspora_in_Turkey-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-The_Formation_of_a_Circassian_Diaspora_in_Turkey_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation conference">Alankuş, Sevda; Taymaz, Erol (2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://khas.academia.edu/SevdaAlankuş/">"The Formation of a Circassian Diaspora in Turkey"</a>. <i>Adyghe (Cherkess) in the 19th Century: Problems of War and Peace</i>. Adygea, Russia: Maikop State Technology University. p.&#160;2<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">4 May</span> 2016</span>. <q>Today, the largest communities of Circassians, about 5–7 million, live in Turkey, and about 200,000 Circassians live in the Middle Eastern countries (Jordan, Syria, Egypt, and Israel). The 1960s and 1970s witnessed a new wave of migration from diaspora countries to Europe and the United States. It is estimated that there are now more than 100,000 Circassian living in the European Union countries. The community in Kosovo expatriated to Adygea after the war in 1998.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=conference&amp;rft.atitle=The+Formation+of+a+Circassian+Diaspora+in+Turkey&amp;rft.btitle=Adyghe+%28Cherkess%29+in+the+19th+Century%3A+Problems+of+War+and+Peace&amp;rft.place=Adygea%2C+Russia&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=Maikop+State+Technology+University&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.aulast=Alanku%C5%9F&amp;rft.aufirst=Sevda&amp;rft.au=Taymaz%2C+Erol&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fkhas.academia.edu%2FSevdaAlanku%C5%9F%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACircassians" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
